Repository_Name O
: O
demigor/lex.db O

Repository_Link O
: O
https://github.com/demigor/lex.db O

Lex.DB O

Lex.DB B-Application
is O
a O
lightweight O
, O
superfast O
, O
in-process O
database O
engine O
, O
completely O
written O
in O
AnyCPU O
C# B-Programming_Language
. O

Why O
? O

We O
feel O
the O
need O
in O
small O
, O
fast O
and O
platform-neutral O
solution O
to O
store O
and O
access O
data O
locally O
. O

SQLite B-Application
is O
almost O
good O
, O
but O
it O
is O
binary O
platform-specific O
( O
x32/x64/ARM O
versions O
of O
SQLite.dll O
) O
, O
and O
has O
no O
real O
support O
for O
Silverlight B-Library
. O

Supported O
platforms O
: O

New O
: O
Xamarin.iOS B-Application
& O
Xamarin.Android B-Application
. O

New O
: O
Universal B-Application
Windows I-Application
Store I-Application
Apps I-Application
Support O

New O
: O
PCL B-Library
version O
for O
supported O
platforms O

.NET B-Library
4.0 B-Version
+ I-Version
, O

Silverlight B-Library
5.0 B-Version
+ I-Version
, O

Windows B-Operating_System
Phone I-Operating_System
8.0 B-Version
+ I-Version
, O

WinRT+ B-Application
. O

Write O
your O
data O
access O
layer O
once O
, O
run O
everywhere O
( O
x64 O
, O
x32 O
, O
ARM O
) O
without O
recompilation O
. O

Lex.DB B-Application
supports O
concurrent O
database O
access O
, O
so O
multiple O
instances O
of O
your O
application O
are O
safe O
to O
go O
( O
.NET B-Library
, O
Silverlight B-Library
) O
. O

Lex.DB B-Application
also O
provides O
both O
synchronous O
and O
asynchronous O
database O
interface O
to O
avoid O
UI O
blockage O
. O

Usage O
is O
greatly O
inspired O
by O
Sterling B-Library
, O
but O
performance O
is O
faster O
than O
native O
SQLite B-Application
. O

Lex.DB.Sync B-Library
- O
lightweight O
data O
synchronization O
framework O
is O
logical O
extensions O
of O
Lex.DB B-Application
. O

Features O
still O
in O
development O

Serialization O
of O
complex O
types O

Serialization O
of O
references O
& O
lists O
of O
references O
( O
one-to-many O
, O
many-to-many O
associations O
) O

Single O
file O
schema O
( O
right O
now O
each O
table B-Data_Structure
has O
two O
files O
: O
index O
and O
data O
) O

Check O
author O
blog O
for O
more O
information O
about O
Lex.DB B-Application
. O

in O
a O
terminal B-Application
. O

Motivation O

I O
would O
like O
to O
add O
new O
tasks O
to O
my O
TaskWarrior B-Application
inbox O
from O
remote O
places O
where O
I O
do O
n't O
have O
immediate O
access O
to O
my O
personal O
TaskWarrior B-Application
database O
; O
e.g O
. O

from O
my O
iPhone B-Device
, O
from O
work O
( O
where O
I O
do O
n't O
have O
access O
to O
my O
personal O
TaskWarrior B-Application
installation O
) O
or O
from O
another O
computer O
. O

Using O
eMail O
for O
this O
looks O
like O
a O
great O
candidate O
: O

I O
do O
n't O
want O
to O
( O
or O
cannot O
) O
install O
TaskWarrior B-Application
on O
all O
the O
places O
and O
machines O
where O
I O
would O
like O
to O
add O
tasks O
from O
. O

Sending O
a O
note O
as O
eMail O
is O
pretty O
much O
universally O
available O
. O

Many O
applications O
were O
not O
made O
for O
integration O
with O
TaskWarrior B-Application
. O

But O
even O
the O
dumbest O
iPhone B-Device
app O
can O
forward O
text O
or O
a O
URL O
via O
eMail O
. O

eMail O
is O
asynchronous O
by O
design O
( O
fire O
and O
forget O
) O
. O

Even O
if O
disconnected O
from O
the O
net O
, O
I O
can O
send O
eMail O
and O
the O
system O
will O
deliver O
it O
on O
the O
very O
next O
occassion O
. O

What O
is O
missing O
from O
a O
TaskWarrior B-Application
perspective O
right O
now O
is O
a O
way O
to O
add O
these O
mails O
to O
a O
TaskWarrior B-Application
installation O
automatically O
. O

Architecture O

The O
simplest O
solution O
I O
could O
come O
up O
with O
is O
this O
: O

A O
dedicated O
email O
account O
is O
used O
to O
collect O
the O
tasks O
. O

A O
script O
that O
imports O
all O
eMails O
as O
new O
tasks O
. O

As O
a O
prerequisite O
, O
TaskWarrior B-Application
is O
assumed O
to O
be O
installed O
and O
configured O
. O

With O
this O
architecture O
in O
place O
, O
the O
functionality O
is O
rather O
simple O
to O
implement O
: O

CODE_BLOCK O
: O
GR_79103 O
( O
code O
omitted O
for O
annotation O
) O

As O
the O
word O
Transaction B-Library_Class
implies O
, O
the O
whole O
operation O
needs O
to O
be O
atomic O
per O
mail O
. O

No O
task O
must O
be O
added O
if O
fetching O
a O
mail O
went O
wrong O
, O
and O
no O
mail O
must O
be O
deleted O
if O
storing O
the O
task O
in O
TaskWarrior B-Application
failed O
. O

The O
solution O
presented O
here O
maintains O
a O
one-to-one O
relation O
between O
the O
INBOX O
of O
an O
mail O
account O
and O
the O
TaskWarrior B-Application
database O
. O

Components O

Mail O
fetching O
is O
done O
with O
fetchmail B-Application
, O
a O
proven O
solution O
available O
on O
all O
major O
Unices B-Operating_System
incl O
. O

MacOS B-Operating_System
. O

It O
will O
be O
configured O
to O
use O
the O
twmail B-Application
script O
as O
a O
mail O
delivery O
agent O
( O
mda O
) O
, O
which O
means O
nothing O
more O
than O
that O
fetchmail B-Application
fetches O
the O
mail O
from O
the O
configured O
account O
and O
hands O
it O
over O
to O
our O
script O
. O

There O
is O
no O
further O
storage O
of O
the O
received O
mails O
except O
in O
TaskWarrior B-Application
. O

Error O
Handling O

If O
our O
MDA O
returns O
non-zero O
, O
fetchmail B-Application
will O
not O
assume O
the O
message O
to O
be O
processed O
and O
it O
will O
try O
again O
. O

Alternatives O

One O
might O
think O
of O
more O
elaborate O
applications O
that O
do O
more O
clever O
things O
, O
but O
I O
wanted O
to O
create O
this O
solution O
with O
as O
few O
external O
dependencies O
as O
possible O
. O

fetchmail B-Application
is O
available O
on O
all O
Unices B-Operating_System
, O
and O
who O
can O
afford O
to O
live O
without O
TaskWarrior B-Application
anyway O
? O

I O
also O
played O
with O
the O
thought O
of O
a O
central O
tasks O
server O
that O
receives O
mail O
from O
services O
like O
CloudMailIn B-Application
and O
auto-adds O
them O
to O
the O
server B-Application
, O
but O
the O
result O
would O
not O
be O
much O
different O
( O
besides O
being O
more O
complex O
) O
to O
the O
solution O
presented O
here O
: O
No O
task O
will O
be O
fetched O
into O
TaskWarrior B-Application
until O
the O
machine O
with O
the O
TaskWarrior B-Application
database O
is O
online O
. O

Another O
alternative O
would O
be O
to O
convert O
the O
email O
to O
JSON B-File_Type
and O
use O
TaskWarrior B-Application
's O
import O
command O
. O

This O
would O
allow O
to O
create O
and O
annotate O
a O
new O
task O
in O
one O
step O
without O
the O
bin/task O
-uuid O
workaround O
. O

Advanced O
Usage O

Filtering O
and O
Routing O

Many O
more O
advanced O
use O
cases O
like O
filtering O
and O
routing O
can O
be O
implemented O
on O
the O
mail O
server B-Application
side I-Application
. O

There O
are O
plenty O
of O
user O
interfaces O
for O
routing O
eMails O
based O
on O
their O
subject O
, O
sender O
, O
body O
text O
, O
etc O
. O

The O
simplest O
way O
to O
integrate O
these O
features O
with O
twmail B-Application
is O
to O
use O
IMAP B-Algorithm
folders O
. O

After O
all O
filtering O
and O

, O

must O
end O
up O
in O
a O
dedicated O
IMAP B-Algorithm

( O
by O
default O
, O

fetched O
from O
the O
INBOX O
folder O
) O
. O

twmail B-Application
can O
then O
be O

to O
do O
different O
things O
depending O
on O
which O
IMAP B-Algorithm
folder O
a O
mail O
came O
from O
. O

As O
an O
example O
, O
here O
is O
a O
simple O
way O
to O
route O
eMails O
to O
different O
projects O
in O
TaskWarrior B-Application
, O

their O

line O
: O

Set O

dedicated O
IMAP B-Algorithm
folder O
for O

you O

on O
, O
e.g O
. O

" O
Build O
Bikeshed O
" O
, O
" O
Reading O
List O
" O
, O
" O
Get O
Rich O
Fast O
" O

Configure O
the O
mail O
server B-Application
to O
move O
every O
mail O
from O
INBOX O
to O
the O

" O
Build O
Bikeshed O
" O

mail O

" O
project:Bikeshed O
" O

" O
Reading O
List O
" O
folder O
if O

contains O
" O
project:Reading O
" O

" O

Rich O
Fast O
" O
folder O
if O

subject O
contains O
" O
project:GetRichFast O
" O

Tell O
twmail B-Application
to O
fetch O
mails O
from O
the O
" O

" O
, O
" O
Reading O
List O

, O

" O
Get O
Rich O
Fast O
" O
IMAP B-Algorithm
folders O

) O
: O

The O

chosen O
for O
twmail B-Application
also O

. O

Handling O
that O

of O
the O
mail O
server B-Application
. O

Anything O
that O

to O

task O
. O

Hooks O

twmail B-Application

. O

This O
makes O

incoming O

, O
and O

is O
no O

to O

twmail B-Application

its O

. O

When O

, O

( O

. O

Within O

, O

: O

CODE_BLOCK O
: O
GR_79104 O
( O
code O
omitted O
for O
annotation O
) O

Have O
a O

. O

If O

For O

Housekeeping O

By O
default O
fetchmail B-Application
will O
mark O
retrieved O
messages O
as O
read O
, O
but O
leave O
them O
on O
the O
server B-Application
. O

For O
housekeeping O
purposes O
, O
it O
may O
be O
desirable O
to O
delete O
messages O
from O
the O
server B-Application
once O
they O
were O
successfully O
imported O
into O
TaskWarrior B-Application
. O

There O
are O
two O
ways O
to O
achieve O
this O
: O

Create O
a O
filter O
on O
the O
server B-Application
side I-Application
that O
deletes O
all O
read O
mail O
to O
a O
dedicated O
folder O
( O
perhaps O
" O
Archive O
" O
or O
" O
Trash O
" O
) O
, O
or O
simply O
deletes O
it O
. O

Run O
fetchmail B-Application
with O
the O
--nokeep O
option O
, O
which O
will O
delete O
retrieved O
messages O
from O
the O
server B-Application
. O

Which O
option O
to O
choose O
depends O
on O
the O
capabilities O
of O
your O
mail O
server B-Application
( O
Google B-Application
Mail I-Application
cannot O
handle O
mails O
based O
on O
their O
read O
status O
) O
, O
and O
on O
your O
level O
of O
trust O
in O
twmail B-Application
. O

I O
recommend O
leaving O
mails O
on O
the O
server B-Application
until O
you O
are O
confident O
that O
everything O
works O
as O
expected O
. O

Testing O

twmail B-Application
comes O
with O
a O
basic O
set O
of O
tests O
. O

Execute O
them O
by O
running O
rake O
in O
the O
cloned O
source O
repo O
. O

New O

imagefs.interact(disk,partitions) O

Returning O

UhOh O

No O

" O

INSTALLATION O

You O
have O
four O
options O
for O
installing O
PASTA B-Application
. O

Windows B-Operating_System
: O
If O
you O
have O
a O
Windows B-Operating_System
machine O
, O
currently O
using O
the O
Docker B-Application
image B-User_Interface_Element
or O
the O
Virtual B-Application
Machine I-Application
( O
VM B-Application
) O
image B-User_Interface_Element
we O
provide O
is O
your O
only O
option O
. O

Among O
those O
two O
options O
, O
Docker B-Application
is O
the O
preferred O
method O
. O

Linux B-Operating_System
: O
If O
you O
have O
Linux B-Operating_System
( O
or O
other O
* B-Operating_System
nix I-Operating_System
systems O
) O
, O
you O
can O
still O
use O
Docker B-Application
or O
VM B-Application
, O
but O
downloading O
the O
code O
from O
github B-Website
and O
installing O
it O
is O
what O
we O
recommend O
. O

MAC B-Operating_System
: O
We O
have O
four O
options O
for O
MAC B-Operating_System
: O
VM B-Application
, O
Docker B-Application
, O
installing O
from O
the O
code O
, O
and O
downloading O
the O
.dmg B-File_Type
file O
. O

If O
you O
mostly O
use O
the O
GUI O
, O
then O
the O
MAC B-Operating_System
.dmg B-File_Type
file O
is O
a O
good O
option O
( O
although O
sometimes O
it O
can O
be O
behind O
the O
latest O
code O
) O
. O

Otherwise O
, O
we O
reocmmend O
either O
Docker B-Application
or O
the O
code O
. O

Common O
Problems O
: O

In O

Options O

PASTA B-Application
estimates O
alignments O
and O
maximum O
likelihood O
( O
ML O
) O
trees B-Data_Structure
from O
unaligned O
sequences O
using O
an O
iterative O
approach O
. O

In O
each O
iteration O
, O
it O
first O
estimates O
a O
multiple O
sequence O
alignment O
and O
then O
a O
ML O
tree B-Data_Structure
is O
estimated O
on O
( O
a O
masked O
version O
of O
) O
the O
alignment O
. O

By O
default O
PASTA B-Application
performs O
3 O
iterations O
, O
but O
a O
host O
of O
options O
enable O
changing O
that O
behavior O
. O

In O
each O
iteration O
, O
a O
divide-and-conquer B-Algorithm
strategy O
is O
used O
for O
estimating O
the O
alignment O
. O

The O
set O
of O
sequences O
is O
divided O
into O
smaller O
subsets O
, O
each O
of O
which O
is O
aligned O
using O
an O
external O
alignment O
tool O
( O
the O
default O
is O
MAFFT-L-ins-i B-Application
) O
. O

These O
subset O
alignments O
are O
then O
pairwise O
merged O
( O
by O
default O
using O
Opal B-Application
) O
and O
finally O
the O
pairwise O
merged O
alignments O
are O
merged O
into O
a O
final O
alignment O
using O
transitivity O
merge O
. O

The O
division O
of O
the O
dataset O
into O
smaller O
subsets O
and O
selecting O
which O

sample_rate_index O
= O
0x1E O

0x1E O
is O
30 O
in O

and O
stands O
for O
30 O
MHz O
. O

The O
modded O
firmware O
and O
custom O

new O

rates O
. O

It O
is O
not O
supported O

stock O

. O

The O
list O
of O
sample O
rates O
is O
: O
10 O
, O
20 O
, O
50 O
= O
100/200/500kHz O
, O
1 O
, O
2 O
, O
4 O
, O
8 O
, O
12 O
, O
16 O
, O
24 O
, O
30 O
, O
48 O
= O
samplerate O
in O
MHz O
. O

48 O
MHz O
does O
n't O
really O
work O
, O
since O
USB B-Device
2.0 B-Version
is O
too O
slow O
. O

It O

seem O
to O

to O

the O
sample_rate O
, O
when O

the O

. O

( O

) O
, O

( O

) O
. O

Is O
this O
a O
limitation O
, O
or O
am O
I O
not O
understanding O
something O
? O

This O
is O
not O
what O
happens O
for O
me O
. O

Did O
you O
install O
the O
modded O
firmware O
, O
or O
the O
custom O
firmware O
? O

Also O
try O
a O
different O

port/hub O
. O

Repository_Name O

diasdavid/interface O
-record-store O

Repository_Link O
: O
https://github.com/diasdavid/interface-record-store O

interface-record-store B-Library


A O
test O
suite O
and O
interface O
you O
can O
use O
to O
implement O
a O
a O
IPRS O
compliant O
Record B-Library
Store I-Library
. O

The O
primary O
goal O
of O
this O
module O
is O
to O
enable O
developers O
to O
pick O
and O
swap O
their O
Record B-Library
Store I-Library
module O
as O
they O
see O
fit O
for O
their O
libp2p B-Library
installation O
, O
without O
having O
to O
go O
through O
shims O
or O
compatibility O
issues O
. O

This O
module O
and O
test O
suite O
were O
heavily O
inspired O
by O
abstract-blob-store B-Library
and O
interface-stream-muxer B-Library
. O

Publishing O
a O
test O
suite O
as O
a O
module O
lets O
multiple O
modules O
all O
ensure O
compatibility O
since O
they O
use O
the O
same O
test O
suite O
. O

The O
API B-Library
is O
presented O
with O
both O
Node.js B-Application
and O
Go B-Programming_Language
primitives O
, O
however O
, O
there O
is O
not O
actual O
limitations O
for O
it O
to O
be O
extended O
for O
any O
other O
language O
, O
pushing O
forward O
the O
cross O
compatibility O
and O
interop O
through O

Repository_Name O
: O
katzer/cordova O
-plugin-background-mode O

Repository_Link O
: O
https://github.com/katzer/cordova-plugin-background-mode O


SAMPLE O
APP O
:point_right O
: O

Cordova B-Library
Background O
Plugin O

Plugin O
for O
the O
Cordova B-Library
framework O
to O
perform O
infinite O
background O
execution O
. O

Most O
mobile B-Device
operating O
systems O
are O
multitasking O
capable O
, O
but O
most O
apps O
dont O
need O
to O
run O
while O
in O
background O
and O
not O
present O
for O
the O
user O
. O

Therefore O
they O
pause O
the O
app O
in O
background O
mode O
and O
resume O
the O
app O
before O
switching O
to O
foreground O
mode O
. O

The O
system O
keeps O
all O
network O
connections O
open O
while O
in O
background O
, O
but O
does O
not O
deliver O
the O
data O
until O
the O
app O
resumes O
. O

Store O
Compliance O

Infinite O
background O
tasks O
are O
not O
official O
supported O
on O
most O
mobile B-Device
operation O
systems O
and O
thus O
not O
compliant O
with O
public O
store O
vendors O
. O

A O
successful O
submssion O
is O
n't O
garanteed O
. O

Use O
the O
plugin O
by O
your O
own O
risk O
! O

Supported O
Platforms O

Android/Amazon B-Operating_System
FireOS I-Operating_System

Browser B-Application

iOS B-Operating_System

Windows B-Operating_System
( O
see O
#222 O
) O

Installation O

The O
plugin O
can O
be O
installed O
via O

- O

Description O

flamejam B-Application
is O
a O
generic O
game O
jam O
application O
that O
uses O
the O
Flask B-Library

. O

It O

for O
any O

game O
jam O

. O

This O
application O
is O
designed O
to O

sure O
that O
participants O

on O
other O

fairly O
and O

. O

Installation O

are O
currently O

to O

. O

This O

Introduction O

This O
second O
programming O
assignment O
will O
require O
you O
to O
write O
an O
R B-Programming_Language
function O
that O
is O
able O
to O
cache O
potentially O
time-consuming O
computations O
. O

For O
example O
, O
taking O
the O
mean O
of O
a O
numeric O
vector B-Data_Structure
is O
typically O
a O
fast O
operation O
. O

However O
, O
for O
a O
very O
long O
vector B-Data_Structure
, O
it O
may O
take O
too O
long O
to O
compute O
the O
mean O
, O
especially O
if O
it O
has O
to O
be O
computed O
repeatedly O
( O
e.g O
. O

in O
a O
loop O
) O
. O

If O
the O
contents O
of O
a O
vector B-Data_Structure
are O
not O
changing O
, O
it O
may O
make O
sense O
to O
cache O
the O
value O
of O
the O
mean O
so O
that O
when O
we O
need O
it O
again O
, O
it O
can O
be O
looked O
up O
in O
the O
cache O
rather O
than O
recomputed O
. O

In O
this O
Programming O
Assignment O
you O
will O
take O
advantage O
of O
the O
scoping O
rules O
of O
the O
R B-Programming_Language
language O
and O
how O
they O
can O
be O
manipulated O
to O
preserve O
state O
inside O
of O
an O
R B-Programming_Language
object O
. O

Example O
: O
Caching O
the O
Mean O
of O
a O
Vector B-Data_Structure

In O
this O
example O
we O
introduce O
the O
<< O
- O
operator O
which O
can O
be O
used O
to O
assign O
a O
value O
to O
an O
object O
in O
an O
environment O
that O
is O
different O
from O
the O
current O
environment O
. O

Below O
are O
two O
functions O
that O
are O
used O
to O
create O
a O
special O
object O
that O
stores O
a O
numeric O
vector B-Data_Structure
and O
caches O
its O
mean O
. O

The O
first O
function O
, O
makeVector O
creates O
a O
special O
" O
vector B-Data_Structure
" O
, O
which O
is O
really O
a O
list B-Data_Structure
containing O
a O
function O
to O

set O
the O
value O
of O
the O
vector B-Data_Structure

get O
the O
value O
of O
the O
vector B-Data_Structure

set O
the O
value O
of O
the O
mean O

get O
the O
value O
of O
the O
mean O

CODE_BLOCK O
: O
GR_3269 O
( O
code O
omitted O
for O
annotation O
) O

The O
following O
function O
calculates O
the O
mean O
of O
the O
special O
" O
vector B-Data_Structure
" O
created O
with O
the O
above O
function O
. O

However O
, O
it O
first O
checks O
to O
see O
if O
the O
mean O
has O
already O
been O
calculated O
. O

If O
so O
, O
it O
gets O
the O
mean O
from O
the O
cache O
and O
skips O
the O
computation O
. O

Otherwise O
, O
it O
calculates O
the O
mean O
of O
the O
data O
and O
sets O
the O
value O
of O
the O
mean O
in O
the O
cache O
via O
the O
setmean O

function O
. O

CODE_BLOCK O
: O
GR_3270 O
( O
code O
omitted O
for O
annotation O
) O

Assignment O
: O
Caching O
the O
Inverse O
of O
a O
Matrix B-Data_Structure

Matrix B-Data_Structure
inversion O
is O
usually O
a O
costly O
computation O
and O
there O
may O
be O
some O
benefit O
to O
caching O
the O
inverse O
of O
a O
matrix B-Data_Structure
rather O
than O
computing O
it O
repeatedly O
( O

are O
also O
alternatives O
to O
matrix B-Data_Structure
inversion O
that O
we O
will O
not O
discuss O
here O
) O
. O

Your O
assignment O
is O
to O
write O
a O
pair O
of O
functions O
that O
cache O
the O
inverse O
of O
a O
matrix B-Data_Structure
. O

Write O
the O
following O
functions O
: O

makeCacheMatrix O
: O
This O
function O
creates O
a O
special O
" O
matrix B-Data_Structure
" O
object O
that O
can O
cache O
its O
inverse O
. O

cacheSolve O
: O
This O
function O
computes O
the O
inverse O
of O
the O
special O
" O
matrix B-Data_Structure
" O
returned O
by O
makeCacheMatrix O
above O
. O

If O
the O
inverse O
has O
already O
been O
calculated O
( O
and O
the O
matrix B-Data_Structure
has O
not O
changed O
) O
, O
then O
cacheSolve O
should O
retrieve O
the O
inverse O
from O
the O
cache O
. O

Computing O
the O
inverse O
of O
a O
square O
matrix B-Data_Structure
can O
be O
done O
with O
the O
solve O

function O
in O
R B-Programming_Language
. O
For O
example O
, O
if O
X O
is O
a O
square O
invertible O
matrix B-Data_Structure
, O
then O

solve(X) O
returns O
its O
inverse O
. O

For O
this O
assignment O
, O
assume O
that O
the O
matrix B-Data_Structure
supplied O
is O
always O
invertible O
. O

In O

this O
assignment O
, O
you O
must O
do O
the O
following O
: O

https://github.com/rdpeng/ProgrammingAssignment2 O

to O

own O
account O
. O

GitHub B-Website
repository O

so O
that O

can O

. O

Edit O

R B-File_Type

#CNN B-Algorithm
TensorFLow B-Library
CIFAR-10 O
is O
a O

in O
machine O

for O

. O

Link O
: O

Overview O

Code O

to O

to O

and O

neural I-Algorithm

( O
CNN B-Algorithm
) O

. O

We O

Model O
Architecture O

The O
model O
in O
this O
CIFAR-10 O
tutorial O
is O
a O
multi-layer O
architecture O
consisting O
of O
alternating O
convolutions O
and O
nonlinearities O
. O

These O
layers O
are O
followed O
by O
fully O
connected O
layers O
leading O
into O
a O
softmax B-Algorithm
classifier O
. O

The O
model O
follows O
the O
architecture O
described O
by O
Alex O
Krizhevsky O
, O
with O
a O
few O
differences O
in O
the O
top O
few O
layers O
. O

This O
model O
achieves O
a O
peak O
performance O
of O
about O
86% O
accuracy O
within O
a O
few O
hours O
of O
training O
time O
on O
a O
GPU B-Device
. O

Please O
see O
below O
and O
the O
code O
for O
details O
. O

It O
consists O
of O
1,068,298 O
learnable O
parameters O
and O
requires O
about O
19.5M O
multiply-add O
operations O
to O
compute O
inference O
on O
a O
single O
image B-User_Interface_Element
. O

Code O
Organization O

File O

Purpose O

cifar10_input.py O

Reads O
the O
native O
CIFAR-10 O
binary B-File_Type
file O
format O
. O

cifar10.py O

Builds O
the O
CIFAR-10 O
model O
. O

cifar10_train.py O

Trains O
a O
CIFAR-10 O
model O
on O
a O
CPU B-Device
or O
GPU B-Device
. O

cifar10_multi_gpu_train.py O

Trains O
a O
CIFAR-10 O
model O
on O
multiple O
GPUs B-Device
. O

cifar10_eval.py O

Evaluates O
the O
predictive O
performance O
of O
CIFAR10 O

CIFAR-10 O
Model O

The O
CIFAR-10 O
network O
is O
largely O
contained O
in O
cifar10.py O
. O

The O
complete O
training O
graph B-Data_Structure
contains O
roughly O
765 O
operations O
. O

We O
find O
that O
we O
can O
make O
the O
code O
most O
reusable O
by O
constructing O
the O
graph B-Data_Structure
with O
the O
following O
modules O
: O

Model O
Inputs O

The O
input O
part O
of O
the O
model O
is O
built O
by O
the O
functions O
inputs() O
and O
distorted_inputs() O
which O
read O
images B-User_Interface_Element
from O
the O
CIFAR-10 O
binary B-File_Type
data O

. O

These O
files O
contain O
fixed O
byte O
length O
records O
, O
so O
we O
use O
tf.FixedLengthRecordReader B-Library_Class
. O

The O
images B-User_Interface_Element
are O
processed O
as O
follows O
: O

CODE_BLOCK O
: O
GR_12118 O
( O
code O
omitted O
for O
annotation O
) O

For O

, O
we O
additionally O
apply O
a O

to O

data O

: O

CODE_BLOCK O
: O
GR_12119 O
( O
code O

) O

Model O
Predicition O

The O
prediction O
part O
of O
the O
model O
is O

by O
the O
inference() O
function O
which O
adds O
operations O
to O

of O

. O

That O
part O
of O
the O
model O
is O
organized O
as O
follows O
: O

Layer O
Name O

Description O

conv1 O

convolution B-Algorithm
and O
rectified B-Algorithm
linear I-Algorithm
activation I-Algorithm
. O

pool1 O

max B-Algorithm
pooling I-Algorithm
. O

conv2 O

convolution B-Algorithm
and O
rectified B-Algorithm
linear I-Algorithm
activation I-Algorithm
. O

norm2 O

local B-Algorithm
response I-Algorithm
normalization I-Algorithm
. O

pool2 O

max B-Algorithm
pooling I-Algorithm
. O

local3 O

fully B-Algorithm
connected I-Algorithm
layer I-Algorithm
with O
rectified B-Algorithm
linear I-Algorithm
activation I-Algorithm
. O

local4 O

fully B-Algorithm
connected I-Algorithm
layer I-Algorithm
with O
rectified B-Algorithm
linear I-Algorithm
activation I-Algorithm
. O

softmax_linear B-Algorithm

linear O
transformation O
to O
produce O
logits O
. O

Model O
Training O

The O
usual O
method O
for O
training O
a O
network O
to O
perform O
N-way O
classification O
is O
multinomial B-Algorithm
logistic I-Algorithm
regression I-Algorithm
, O
aka O
. O

softmax B-Algorithm
regression I-Algorithm
. O

Softmax B-Algorithm
regression I-Algorithm
applies O
a O
softmax B-Algorithm
nonlinearity I-Algorithm
to O
the O
output O
of O
the O
network O
and O
calculates O
the O
cross-entropy B-Algorithm
between O
the O
normalized O
predictions O
and O
a O
1-hot B-Algorithm
encoding I-Algorithm
of O
the O
label O
. O

For O
regularization O
, O
we O
also O
apply O
the O
usual O
weight O
decay O
losses O
to O
all O
learned O
variables O
. O

The O
objective O
function O
for O
the O
model O
is O
the O
sum O
of O
the O
cross B-Algorithm
entropy I-Algorithm
loss I-Algorithm
and O
all O
these O
weight O
decay O
terms O
, O
as O
returned O
by O
the O
loss() O
function O
. O

Redmine B-Application
Airbrake I-Application
Plugin O

This O
plugin O

It O

I O
've O
got O
48M O
datapoints O
. O

I O
've O
noticed O
, O
that O
in O
my O
case O
( O
Voltrage O
range O
-2.5V O
to O
+ O
2.5V O
) O

, O

" O
-2.5 O
" O
. O

So O

to O
delete O
these O
values O
, O
I O
'm O
left O

a O
fine O

. O

The O

, O
that O
every O
second O

, O

need O
e.g O
. O

with O
200Ks O
only O
400.000 O
data O
points O
. O

So O
the O
limit O
on O
my O
computer B-Device
is O
around O
15 O
seconds O
- O
he O
needs O
like O
a O
minute O
to O
save O
the O
data O
. O

Any O
longer O
time O
period O
results O
in O
a O
program O
crash O
. O

Generally O
I O
just O
want O
to O
record O
data O
for O
about O
2 O
minutes O
with O
a O
sample O
rate O
of O
200-500Ks O
for O

simultaneously O
and O

. O

Plotting O
and O

then O
is O
done O
with O
R B-Programming_Language
. O

, O

webpack-sandboxed B-Application

on O

, O

. O

. O

Flexgrid B-Application
- O
a O
simple O
grid O
based O
on O
flexbox B-Library
layout O

No O
more O
floats O
! O

Regular O
grid O
layout O
is O
based O
on O
both O
block O
and O
inline O
flow O
directions O
, O
however O
, O
the O
flexbox B-Library
( O
or O
just O
flex B-Library
) O
layout O
is O
based O
on O
" O
flex-flow O
directions O
" O
. O

Thus O
float O
and O
clear O
have O
no O
effect O
. O

Using O
float O
causes O
the O
display-property O
to O
compute O
to O
block O
. O

Using O
flexbox B-Library
also O
means O
less O
JavaScript B-Version
! O

Everything O
is O
, O
of O
course O
, O
responsive O
and O
stacks O
perfectly O
. O

Please O
note O
: O
Flexbox B-Library
is O
only O
partially O
supported O
by O
IE10 B-Application
. O

Any O
IE-version B-Application
lower O
than O
10 B-Version
does O
not O
support O
flexbox O
. O

However O
, O
Flexgrid B-Application
has O
many O
fallbacks O
included O
, O
so O
IE11 B-Application
should O
be O
safe O
. O

More O
info O
here O
. O

Flexgrid B-Library
is O
an O
integral O
part O
of O
the O
upcoming O
Nano B-Library
Framework I-Library
, O
where O
Flexgrid B-Library
is O
the O
standard O
grid-system O
and O
provides O
a O
stable O
flexbox B-Library
skeleton O
. O

Demo O

A O
live O
demo O
is O
available O
here O
: O
DEMO O

you O
want O
to O

or O

.container O

.container-fluid O

Flexgrid B-Application
comes O
with O
responsive O
containers O
that O
boxes O
the O
content O
in O
which O
are O
controlled O
by O
@media O
-queries O
. O

These O
@media O
-queries O
trigger O
at O
the O
same O
widths O
defined O
by O
the O
Bootstrap-framework B-Library
. O

However O
, O
as O

small O
detail O
, O
Flexgrid B-Application
bases O
its O
width-triggers O
on O
rem O
instead O
of O
px O
. O

This O
creates O
a O
much O
more O
fluid O
layout O
. O

While O
em O
is O
relative O
to O
the O
font-size O
of O
its O
direct O
or O
nearest O
parent O
, O
rem O
is O
only O
relative O
to O
the O
html B-Programming_Language
( O
root O
) O
font-size O
. O

Flexgrid B-Application
font-size O
is O
set O
to O
16px O
. O

There O
is O
also O
a O
fluid O
container O
that O
has O
no O
@media O
-queries O
. O

Intro O

Fieldtop B-Application
looks O
at O
all O
fields O
in O
all O
tables B-Data_Structure
and O
all O
databases O
and O
analyzes O
how O
close O
the O
values O
in O

field O
are O
to O
the O
maximum O
( O
or O
minimum O
) O
allowed O
value O
for O
the O
given O
field O
type O
. O

This O
can O
give O
you O
interesting O
insight O
into O
your O
databases O
. O

A O
typical O
output O
looks O
like O
this O
: O

Field O

Min O

Max O

community.users.id O

30% O

community.users.name O

100% O

community.users.karma O

60% O

1% O

community.posts.id O

1% O

community.posts.text O

100% O

This O
would O
tell O
you O
a O
couple O
of O
things O
at O
a O
glance O
: O

Your O
user O
IDs O
use O
30% O
of O
the O
available O
range O
. O

Depending O
on O
how O
long O

project O
has O
been O

, O
this O
can O
be O
ok O
or O
could O

field O
is O

danger O
of O
overflowing O
at O
some O
point O
. O

Some O
user O
names O
already O
use O
the O
maximum O
length O
. O

This O
is O
probably O
ok O
if O
your O
database O
design O
is O
in O
sync O
with O
your O
application O
. O

The O
negative O
values O
in O
the O
user O
karma O
column O
are O
already O
pretty O
big O
. O

Maybe O
you O
did O

expect O
that O
people O
aquire O
negative O
karma O
so O
fast O
? O

The O
IDs O
for O
posts O
are O
far O
from O

limit O

The O
text O
field O
for O
the O
posts O
is O
already O
maxing O
out O
the O
max O
lenght O
. O

Maybe O
that O
is O
not O
what O
you O
want O
. O

The O
output O
can O

escpecially O
interesting O
for O
databases O
that O
have O

used O

extended O

. O

Often O

some O

, O

the O
data O

designated O
data O
types O
. O

In O

, O

when O
no-gravity O
noticed O
that O

, O

maxed O

Repository_Name O
: O
alexgorbatchev/fork O
-promise O

Repository_Link O
: O
https://github.com/alexgorbatchev/fork-promise O

fork-promise O

Executes O
code O
in O
a O
forked O
Node.js B-Application
process O
and O
returns O
a O
Bluebird B-Library_Class
promise I-Library_Class
. O

This O
is O
useful O
for O
parallelizing O
heavy O
tasks O
and O
taking O
advantage O
of O
multiple O
CPUs/cores B-Device
. O

Please O
note O
, O
this O
is O
only O
useful O
for O
splitting O
up O
long O
running O
tasks O
because O
according O
to O
the O
doc O
: O

These O
child O
Nodes O
are O
still O
whole O
new O
instances O
of O
V8 B-Version
. O

Assume O
at O
least O
30ms O
startup O
and O
10mb O
memory O
for O
each O
new O
Node O
. O

That O
is O
, O
you O
cannot O
create O
many O
thousands O
of O
them O
. O

: O

( O

for O
annotation O
) O

Usage O
Example O

the O
example O
below O
the O
job O
function O
will O
be O
executed O
in O
a O
forked O
process O
. O

Please O
note O
there O
is O
parent O
scope O
access O
and O
the O
job O
function O
is O
executed O
in O
the O
global O
context O
of O
the O
new O
process O
. O

This O

. O

, O
as O

as O

. O

‚úÖ O
If O

This O

. O

‚ùå O

. O

simple O
game O
built O
with O
JavaScript B-Programming_Language
and O
jQuery B-Library
where O
users O
flip O
cards O
and O
look O
for O
matches O

Description O
: O

Concentration O
, O
also O
known O
as O
Match O
Match O
, O
Memory O
, O
Pelmanism O
, O
Shinkei-suijaku O
, O
Pexeso O
or O
simply O
Pairs O
, O
is O
a O
card O
game O
in O
which O
all O
of O
the O
cards O
are O
laid O
face O
down O
on O
a O
surface O
and O
two O
cards O
are O
flipped O
face O
up O
over O
each O
turn O
. O

The O
object O
of O
the O
game O
is O
to O
turn O
over O
pairs O
of O
matching O
cards O

Notes O
: O

Plans O
for O
the O
future O
will O
allow O
for O
random O
card O
placement O
and O
smoother O
animations O

Hi O
Nada O
, O

The O
config B-File_Type
files O
in O
pasta B-Application
have O
to O
be O
in O
a O
valid O
INI B-File_Type
file O
format O
, O
specifically O
the O
structure O
used O
by O
the O
python B-Programming_Language
configparser B-Library_Class
module O
( O
see O
https://docs.python.org/3/library/configparser.html O
) O
. O

So O
the O
most O
likely O
issue O
is O
that O
some O
part O
of O
the O
cfg B-File_Type
file O
did O
not O
conform O
to O
those O
specs O
. O

In O
the O
case O
of O
PASTA B-Application
, O
it O
will O
be O
looking O
for O
specific O
section O
and O
key O
names O
. O

The O
best O
way O
to O
create O
a O
config B-File_Type
file O
might O
be O
to O
run O
pasta B-Application
on O
one O
of O
the O
examples O
and O
look O
at O
the O
config B-File_Type
file O
that O
is O
created O
in O
the O
output O
folder O
. O

That O
will O
be O
populated O
by O
default O
settings O
( O
excpet O
for O
things O
like O
input O
and O
output O
paths O
and O
such O
) O
. O

But O
using O
that O
as O
a O
template O
for O
a O
new O
config B-File_Type
file O
should O
be O
helpful O
. O

Let O
me O
know O
if O
that O
does O
n't O
help O
. O

Mike O

Creating O

count O

( O

) O

The O
-s O

of O

, O

to O

. O

The O

If O

, O

of O

: O

CODE_BLOCK O
: O
GR_27477 O
( O
code O
omitted O
for O
annotation O
) O

or O

CODE_BLOCK O
: O
GR_27478 O
( O
code O
omitted O
for O
annotation O
) O

If O

This O

, O

Beware O

The O

. O

bin O
instead O
of O
combining O
them O
into O
MultiPolygons B-Library_Class
. O

-P O
: O
Output O
Points B-Library_Class
or O
MultiPoints B-Library_Class
instead O
of O
Polygons B-Library_Class
or O
MultiPolygons B-Library_Class

Tile O
size O

-k O
: O
Do O
n't O
enforce O
the O
500K O
limit O
on O
tile O
size O

-K O
: O
Raise O
the O
minimum O
count O
threshold O
on O
each O
tile O
if O
necessary O
to O
keep O
it O
under O
500K O
. O

Miscellaneous O
controls O

-p O
cpus O
: O
Use O
the O
specified O
number O
of O
parallel O
tasks O
. O

-q O
: O
Silence O
the O
progress O
indicator O

-B O
multiplier O
: O
Multiply O
the O
normalized O
density O
by O
the O
specified O
multiplier O
to O
make O
it O
brighter O
or O
dimmer O
. O

Relationship O
between O
bin O
size O
, O
maxzoom O
, O
and O
detail O

What O
exactly O
the O
" O
detail O
" O
parameter O
means O
is O
often O
the O
source O
of O
confusion O
. O

It O
is O
the O
difference O
between O
the O
maxzoom O
and O
the O
bin O
size O
. O

So O
, O
for O
example O
, O
if O
you O
have O
data O
with O
a O
bin O
size O
of O
23 O
and O
want O
to O
tile O
it O
with O
a O
maxzoom O
of O
16 O
, O
you O
should O
specify O
a O
detail O
of O
7 O
, O
because O
16+7 O
= O
23 O
. O

Within O
each O
tile O
, O
the O
resolution O
of O
the O
tile O
is O
2^detail O
, O
so O
if O
you O
specify O
a O
detail O
of O
7 O
, O
each O
tile O
will O
be O
a O
128x128 O
grid O
of O
pixels O
or O
features O
, O
because O
2^7 O
= O
128 O
. O

It O
is O
often O
more O
useful O
to O
work O
backward O
from O
the O
bin O
size O
to O
the O
maxzoom O
: O
if O
you O
have O
data O
with O
a O
bin O
size O
of O
24 O
, O
and O
you O
want O
256x256 O
tiles O
, O
2^8 O
= O
256 O
so O
you O
should O
specify O
a O
detail O
of O
8 O
, O
and O
the O
maxzoom O
will O
be O
16 O
because O
24-8 O
= O
16 O
. O

Internal O
file O
format O

The O
.count B-File_Type
files O
contain O
a O
header O
for O
versioning O
and O
identification O
followed O
( O
currently O
) O
by O
a O
simple O
list O
of O
12-byte O
records O
containing O
: O

64-bit O
location O
quadkey O

32-bit O
count O

Repository_Name O
: O
rpcope1/Hantek6022API O

Issue_Event_Link O
: O
https://github.com/rpcope1/Hantek6022API/issues/33 O

( O
python-libusb1 B-Library
author O
here O
) O
I O
am O
surprised O
that O
USBPollerThread B-Library_Class
causes O
lockups O
. O

Rather O
than O
being O
linked O
to O
linux B-Operating_System
version O
, O
it O
should O
be O
either O
linked O
to O
libusb B-Library
version O
( O
the O
C B-Programming_Language
library O
) O
, O
or O
be O
" O
just O
" O
a O
bug O
in O
my O
python B-Programming_Language
wrapper O
. O

The O
issue O
with O
mixing O
sync O
and O
async B-Library
libusb I-Library
APIs I-Library
is O
that O
sync O
API B-Library
is O
just O
" O
start O
async O
call O
and O
handle O
at O
least O
one O
event O
" O
. O

As O
a O
result O
, O
an O
" O
handle O
any O
event O
" O
running O
in O
another O
thread O
may O
" O
steal O
" O
the O
event O
, O
process O
it O
and O
the O
sync O
call O
gets O
stuck O
waiting O
forever O
- O
which O
is O
very O
likely O
the O
case O
here O
. O

USBPollerThread B-Library_Class
works O
around O
this O
by O
implementing O
( O
hopefully O
correctly O
) O
the O
documented O
sequence O
. O

The O
implementation O
in O
USBPollerThread B-Library_Class
differs O
in O
2 O
ways O
from O
the O
documented O
code O
which O
make O
comparison O
a O
bit O
harder O
but O
should O
have O
no O
effect O
: O

Poller B-Library_Class
thread O
does O
not O
need O
to O
check O
a O
" O
completed O
" O
value O
as O
it O
must O
not O
exit O
after O
processing O
a O
specific O
event O
, O
but O
must O
hang O
around O

Repository_Name O

Repository_Link O

orderup O

A O
slack B-Website
bot O
to O
serve O
orders O
like O
a O
restaurant O
, O
give O
people O
an O
order O
number O
, O
cook O
things O
in O
serial O
, O
and O
mark O
orders O
complete O
after O
you O
serve O
them O
. O

Why O
? O

We O
are O
busy O
. O

It O
makes O
us O
grumpy O
sometimes O
. O

And O
when O
people O
interrupt O
us O
on O
slack B-Website
, O
we O
get O
even O
grumpier O
. O

We O
lose O
context O
, O
and O
we O
start O
to O
forget O
what O
we O
were O
doing O
last O
. O

Things O
fall O
on O
the O
floor O
. O

We O
could O
just O
use O
a O
ticketing O
system O
, O
and O
tell O
people O
to O
file O
a O
ticket O
, O
but O
the O
culture O
of O
slack O
is O
n't O
like O
that O
. O

We O
like O
doing O
things O
in O
real O
time O
, O
and O
we O
encourage O
some O
degree O
of O
interruptions O
and O
impromptu O
conversations O
. O

But O
we O
do O
need O
some O
order O
to O
the O
madness O
, O
and O
a O
queue O
makes O
sense O
. O

It O
's O
better O
than O
" O
I O
'm O
busy O
, O
get O
lost O
. O
" O

It O
's O
more O

" O

's O

I O
'm O
up O
to O
, O
you O
're O
next O
. O
" O

So O
we O
built O
orderup O
. O

It O
's O
just O
like O
a O
restaurant O
. O

When O
someone O
asks O
you O
for O
something O
, O
you O
give O

an O
order O
number O
, O
cook O
something O
up O
and O
serve O

to O
them O
. O

Your O
burger O
will O
be O
ready O
after O
I O
make O
fries O
for O
that O
guy O
over O
there O
. O

Now O
replace O
burger O
and O
fries O
with O
insurance O
quote O
, O
git B-Application
commit O
, O
phone O
call O
, O

. O

Repository_Name O

Glome B-Application
Notification I-Application
Broker I-Application
( O
GNB B-Application
) O

GNB B-Application
is O
a O
simple O
message O
broker O
written O
in O
Node.js B-Application
. O

It O
sits O
between O
Glome B-Application
's O
Redis B-Application
server I-Application
and O
the O
web O
clients O
connecting O
via O
websockets O
( O
or O
HTTP O
) O
. O

GNB B-Application
establishes O
two O
connections O
to O
the O
Redis B-Application
server I-Application
for O
duplex O
communication O
. O

One O
of O
the O
connections O
is O
the O
downlink O
that O
carries O
messages O
from O
Glome B-Application
towards O
the O
clients O
. O

The O
other O
connection O
is O
the O
uplink O
that O
transfers O
messages O
from O
the O
clients O
towards O
Glome B-Application
. O

Installation O

: O

( O
code O

annotation O
) O

command O
will O

. O

: O

annotation O
) O

broker O

, O
ie O
. O

listening O

. O

. O

. O

T0 O
is O
timer O
0 O
input O
clock O
. O

So O

count O
the O
pulses O
and O
trigger O
a O

a O
specified O
number O
of O

. O

related O

I O
think O

should O
be O
triggerred O
by O
either O

CTL2 B-Device
. O

MHz O

on O

CTL2 B-Device
to O
1 O
. O

Lower O
modi O
switch O
CTL2 B-Device
in O
the O
wave O
form O
for O
every O
sample O
and O
disable O
clock O
output O
in O

. O

Are O
you O
sure O
CTL2 B-Device
is O
not O
connected O
? O

In O
stock O

24 O
MHz O
was O
broken O
and O
sampled O
with O
48 O
MHz O
, O
while O

with O
16 O
MHz O
( O
ok O
, O

after O

the O
right O
waveform O
) O
. O

The O
result O
was O

were O
always O
3 O

, O

should O
have O
effects O
. O

#Contributing O

Carrasco B-Application

Heartless O

script O

. O

Simple O

, O
yaml B-Programming_Language

file O

Well O
